  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fa49d2f4-55c0-4a82-ad3f-fde03fe35f8a'
      });

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer2396465943410931836">In Barcelona, an aging Brazilian prostitute trains her dog to weep at the grave she has chosen for herself. In Geneva, an ambulance driver and his wife take in the lonely, apparently dying ex-President of a Caribbean country, only to discover that his political a</span>
  <span id="freeText2396465943410931836" style="display:none">In Barcelona, an aging Brazilian prostitute trains her dog to weep at the grave she has chosen for herself. In Vienna, a woman parlays her gift for seeing the future into a fortunetelling position with a wealthy family. In Geneva, an ambulance driver and his wife take in the lonely, apparently dying ex-President of a Caribbean country, only to discover that his political ambition is very much intact. <br /><br />In these twelve masterful short stories about the lives of Latin Americans in Europe, García Márquez conveys the peculiar amalgam of melancholy, tenacity, sorrow, and aspiration that is the émigré experience.</span>

It is full of great stories, however I found some of them kind of soulless, while others are amazing and surprising, with a well<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I just read the book. It is full of great stories, however I found some of them kind of soulless, while others are amazing and surprising, with a well-paced rythm. The best was to be identified in some of the stories, because as a Latin guy I lived in Europe for almost three years: GGM was reading my mind!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

  <span id="freeText17724601919623822883" style="display:none">Doce cuentos peregrinos =‎ Bon voyage Mr. President and other stories = Strange Pilgrims: Twelve stories‭‬‭‬, Gabriel Garcí­a Márquez <br /><br />In Barcelona, an aging Brazilian prostitute trains her dog to weep at the grave she has chosen for herself. In Vienna, a woman parlays her gift for seeing the future into a fortunetelling position with a wealthy family. In Geneva, an ambulance driver and his wife take in the lonely, apparently dying ex-President of a Caribbean country, only to discover that his political ambition is very much intact.<br /><br />عنوانها: قدیس؛ سفر خوش آقای‌ رئیس جمهور و بیست‌ و یک‌ داستان‌ دیگر؛ سفر به‌ خیر آقای‌ رئیس جمهور؛ زائران‌ غریب: دوازده‌ داستان‌؛ زنی‌ که‌ هر روز راس ساعت‌ شش‌ صبح میآمد؛ نویسنده: گابریل گارسیا مارکز؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و پنجم ماه ژوئن سال 1995 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: سفر خوش آقای‌ رئیس جمهور و بیست‌ و یک‌ داستان‌ دیگر؛ نویسنده: گابریل گارسیا مارکز؛ مترجم: احمد گلشیری؛ تهران، نشر نگاه، 1373، در 354 ص؛ شابک: 9646736009؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان کلمبیایی - سده 20 م<br /><br />عنوان: قدیس؛ نویسنده: گابریل گارسیا مارکز؛ مترجم: قهرمان نورانی؛ تهران، سمیر، قائد، 1379؛ در 248 ص؛ چاپ دیگر: تهران، آریابان، 1384؛ چاپ چهارم 1384؛ پنجم 1386؛ ششم 1388؛ هفتم 1389؛ هشتم 1391؛ نهم 1391؛ <br /><br />عنوان: سفر به‌ خیر آقای‌ رئیس جمهور؛ نویسنده: گابریل گارسیا مارکز؛ مترجم: فرزام حبیبی اصفهانی؛ تهران، چلچله، 1392، در 200 ص؛ شابک 978600791556؛ <br /><br />عنوان: زائران‌ غریب: دوازده‌ داستان‌؛ نویسنده: گابریل گارسیا مارکز؛ مترجم: صفدر تقی زاده؛ تهران، مرغ آمین، 1373، در 247 ص؛ چاپ دوم 1373؛ چاپ سوم 1376؛ شابک: 9645519004؛ <br /><br />عنوان: زنی‌ که‌ هر روز راس ساعت‌ شش‌ صبح میآمد؛ نویسنده: گابریل گارسیا مارکز؛ مترجم: نیکتا تیموری؛ تهران، نشر شیرین، 1378، در 160 ص؛ چاپ دوم 1379؛ شابک: 9645564395؛ چاپ دیگر: تهران، آریابان، 1361؛ چاپ هفتم 1389؛<br /><br />نام مجموعه به اسپانیائی: زائران غریب؛ است. و با عنوانهای: سفر به خیر آقای رئیس جمهور و بیست و یک داستان دیگر؛ و قدیس نیز انتشار یافته است و چهارمین مجموعهٔ داستان‌های کوتاه این نویسنده ی پرآوازه است. آنچه این اثر را از سایر آثار مارکز متمایز می‌سازد، محل رخدادها و فضای داستان هاست. داستان‌های این مجموعه، بدبیاری‌های مردمان آمریکای لاتین، در مکان‌هایی دوردست، و در اروپا را تصویر می‌کند؛ و نویسنده با الهام از حرفهٔ روزنامه‌ نگاری - که برایش بسیار ارجمند است - با گذری از نئورئالیسم، به نئورئالیسم جادویی؛ خاطرات اعجاب آور خویش را به رشته ی تحریر می‌کشد. وجود شخصیت‌هایی چون پابلو نرودا، چزاره زاواتینی؛ و دیگران، در متن داستان، این باور را ثابت میکند. خود مارکز در مصاحبه‌ ای گفته است «-این داستان‌ها قطعاً، قطعاتی از خاطرات خود من هستند، که آن‌ها را از دفتر گمشده‌ ام، بازسازی و بازآفرینی کرده‌ ام.»؛ دوازده داستان از داستانهای این سری: قدیس؛ سفر به خیر، آقای رئیس جمهور!؛ زیبای خفته! در هواپیما؛ نور، مثلِ آب است؛ بادِ شمال؛ وحشتِ ماهِ اوت؛ ماریا پراسرس؛ حرفهٔ من خواب دیدن است؛ فقط برای تلفن زدن آمده‌ ام؛ هفده انگلیسی مسموم؛ تابستان خوش خانم «فوریس»؛ لکه‌های خون روی برف. ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_2889093629" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2889093629" />
    <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea"><img alt="Amalia Gkavea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559158764p2/56789747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2889093629?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amalia Gkavea" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea">Amalia Gkavea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=colombia">colombia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=1970s">1970s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=world-culture">world-culture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=south-america">south-america</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=world-literature">world-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=1980s">1980s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2889093629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15323455522906130427"><i>
  <b>‘’A continent conceived by the scum of the earth without a moment of love: the children of abductions, rapes, violations, infamous dealings, deceptions, the union of enemies with enemies.’’</b>
</i><br/><br/>Father of Magical Realism, a true god of Literature, one of the immortals. Gabriel Garcia Márquez doesn’t need introductions. He is the writer who drew my attention to Latin American Literature. Through his work, I fell in love with Colombia, its culture and traditions, with the rich literary world of Cent</span>
  <span id="freeText15323455522906130427" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>‘’A continent conceived by the scum of the earth without a moment of love: the children of abductions, rapes, violations, infamous dealings, deceptions, the union of enemies with enemies.’’</b>
</i><br /><br />Father of Magical Realism, a true god of Literature, one of the immortals. Gabriel Garcia Márquez doesn’t need introductions. He is the writer who drew my attention to Latin American Literature. Through his work, I fell in love with Colombia, its culture and traditions, with the rich literary world of Central and South America. This collection is one more example of the impact and wonder of his writing. <br /><br />12 stories. 12 pilgrims whose life led them away from their homelands into the old, safe arms of Europe. But is it so? Can you ever truly leave your birthplace behind? The answer is ‘’no’’. It is in your blood, your thoughts, your behaviour. It haunts your steps, it doesn’t let go...It doesn’t matter whether you are in Paris, Geneva, Madrid, Barcelona, Naples, Sicily, Rome. Your land is inside you. Everything else is only a pilgrimage…<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Bon Voyage, Mr. President</b>
</i>: A young couple befriends the exiled President of an unnamed Carribean country. Initially their purpose isn’t exactly honest but what happens when he actually manages to gain their sympathy? Set in Barcelona.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>‘’No one sang or died of love in the plastic trattories on the Piazza di Spagna. For the Rome of our memory was by now another ancient Rome within the ancient Rome of the Caesars. Then a voice that might have come from the beyond stopped me cold on a narrow street in Trastevere. ‘’Hello, Poet’’.</b>
</i><br /><br /><i>
  <b>The Saint</b>
</i>: A tender story of a man who has suffered a terrible loss set in Rome, the Eternal City with the immortal beauty, over a sad summer. A story of Art, hope and...self-canonization.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Sleeping Beauty and the Airplane</b>
</i>: A beautiful, heartfelt story of unrequited love at first sight, at Charles de Gaulle Airport in Paris. Márquez transforms a simple, uneventful meeting into pure Art.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>I Sell My Dreams</b>
</i>: An extraordinary story of a woman who had the ability of prophesying through dreams, set in Havana, Vienna and Barcelona. And we get to meet Pablo Neruda.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>‘’Love is eternal for as long as it lasts.’’</b>
</i><br /><br /><i>
  <b>I Only Came to Use the Phone</b>
</i>: A young woman finds herself in an asylum and her real-life nightmare begins somewhere in the Spanish desert. A harrowing story.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>‘’They say this is the country of the Moors’’, said another, distant voice that resounded throughout the dormitory. And it must be true, because in the summer, when there’s a moon, you can hear the dogs barking at the sea.’’</b>
</i><br /><br /><i>
  <b>The Ghosts of August</b>
</i>: A haunted castle in Tuscany is the summer destination of a beautiful family. And this is how you scare the bloody daylights out of a reader in just three pages…<br /><br /><i>
  <b>‘’At Christmas, coloured lights were strung between the acacias, and music and happy voices were heard from the balconies, and a crowd of tourists invaded the sidewalk cafés, but in the midst of all the festivities one could feel the same repressed tension that preceded the days when the anarchists had taken over the streets.’’</b>
</i><br /><br /><i>
  <b>Maria dos Prazeres</b>
</i>: A former prostitute is obsessed with what she perceives to be her impending death. A beautiful, sad story in majestic Barcelona.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Seventeen Poisoned Englishmen</b>
</i>: A woman travels to Naples to see the Pope and witnesses a strange, macabre incident. A fascinating mixture of comedy, mystery and drama.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Tramontana</b>
</i>: A story that vaguely reminded me of Chronicle of a Death Foretold. Brilliant…<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Miss Forbes’s Summer of Happiness</b>
</i>: Two children have to spend their vacations under the control of an extremely strict nanny who has a few dark secrets of her own. Set in Sicily.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Light Is Like Water</b>
</i>: Two boys from Cartagena who adore the sea feel trapped in their small apartment in Madrid. The solution they come up with in order to learn how to row has tragic results…<br /><br /><i>
  <b>‘’She made her mental calculations, and only then realized that they had passed Bordeaux, as well as Angoulême and Poitiers, and were driving along the flooded dike of the Loire. Moonlight filtered through the mist, and the silhouettes of castles through the pines seemed to come from fairy tales.’’</b>
</i><br /><br /><i>
  <b>The Trail of Your Blood In the Snow</b>
</i>: A young married couple drives from the Pyrenees to Paris. The woman has an almost invisible scratch on her ring finger, but she is bleeding, leaving tears of blood in the snow...This is one of the most beautiful, foreboding stories I’ve ever read. It shocks you and leaves you empty and in pain. Actual, physical pain…<br /><br />Gabriel Garcia Márquez writes about exile, despair, loss, shattered hopes, broken families. And death. His pilgrims are people of all walks of life, their backgrounds varying, their aspirations remaining the same. In morbid twists and shocking closures, the reader completes a difficult pilgrimage in the land of the human soul that searches for the unattainable and the pure…<br /><br /><i>
  <b>‘’It is not true that people stop pursuing dreams because they grow old, they grow old because they stop pursuing dreams.’’<br /> Gabriel Garcia Márquez</b>
</i><br /><br />My reviews can also be found on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://theopinionatedreaderblog.wordpress.com">https://theopinionatedreaderblog.word...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15323455522906130427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_41530535" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41530535" />
    <a title="Fabian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1036893-fabian"><img alt="Fabian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514061293p2/1036893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/41530535?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fabian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fabian" href="/user/show/1036893-fabian">Fabian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788497592444" href="/book/show/859860.Doce_cuentos_peregrinos">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41530535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5906209050842858024">I've only read "One Hundred Years", which is beyond a doubt a true masterpiece. <br/><br/>Here, some stories seem irregular. Thats about all I can find as detriment to this clever collection of short (some EXTREMELY so) stories. They all have several things in common: the protagonists are Latinoamericanos in olde Europa. The settings pan around the continent from Madrid to the Spanish coast, London, France, Italia... etc. The prose is good enough to inspire one to fly over there post haste... everything j</span>
  <span id="freeText5906209050842858024" style="display:none">I've only read "One Hundred Years", which is beyond a doubt a true masterpiece. <br /><br />Here, some stories seem irregular. Thats about all I can find as detriment to this clever collection of short (some EXTREMELY so) stories. They all have several things in common: the protagonists are Latinoamericanos in olde Europa. The settings pan around the continent from Madrid to the Spanish coast, London, France, Italia... etc. The prose is good enough to inspire one to fly over there post haste... everything just seems so poetic and life-altering there. (sigh)<br /><br />Also, most of the vignettes deal with an all-time favorite theme: death. Most of the citizens of the book are not youngsters &amp; probably reflect the author's own feelings of antiquity and age.<br /><br />I did like seven or so tales intensely, but some others feel like quack intros to potentially amazing plots. Instead of keeping with the ideas to elongate them into other full-length masterwork novels, Garcia Marquez seems, well, censored (?). <br /><br />Reading this in Spanish makes a HUGE difference, I believe, to the overall experience. The rhetoric is often times untranslateable, and I believe that the English transfer would probably be less rich in prose, as the author loves to sprinkle Spanish sayings and laugh-inducing wit into the melting pot. The lack of overall fantastic elements (such as in, say "100 Years") is sometimes kind of a downer.<br /><br />I say: Good, but probably not a milestone for the author nor, as is usually the case with Marquez's contribution to globe-wide lit, one Truly Remarkable work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5906209050842858024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/22698628" />
    <a title="Rhys" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1138007-rhys"><img alt="Rhys" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442456315p2/1138007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/22698628?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rhys" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rhys" href="/user/show/1138007-rhys">Rhys</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of magic realism</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22698628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15917718886285151667">A truly superb short story collection. I love the short stories of Marquez and his later pieces are even better than his earlier tales. This book features twelve stories written between 1976 and 1982. The first story, 'Bon Voyage, Mr President', states the general theme of those that follow: Latin American citizens adrift (or trapped) in Europe.<br/><br/>Some of the stories are more fantastical than others. Two of the best are also two of the most kafkaesque: 'I Only Came to Use the Phone' and 'The Trail </span>
  <span id="freeText15917718886285151667" style="display:none">A truly superb short story collection. I love the short stories of Marquez and his later pieces are even better than his earlier tales. This book features twelve stories written between 1976 and 1982. The first story, 'Bon Voyage, Mr President', states the general theme of those that follow: Latin American citizens adrift (or trapped) in Europe.<br /><br />Some of the stories are more fantastical than others. Two of the best are also two of the most kafkaesque: 'I Only Came to Use the Phone' and 'The Trail of your Blood in the Snow', both of which feature unwilling incarceration in hospitals. The latter story is heartwrenching as well as disturbing and written in exquisite prose.</span>

<div id="review_697045376" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/697045376" />
    <a title="Pvw" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4377693-pvw"><img alt="Pvw" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291127389p2/4377693.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/697045376?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pvw" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pvw" href="/user/show/4377693-pvw">Pvw</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4377693-pvw?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4377693-pvw?shelf=nostalgia">nostalgia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer697045376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18265563903434714752">Marquez remains a great writer. While not every story in this bundle is equally enjoyable, they all show great mastery and the ability to draw interesting characters in a few lines, a feat in which some writers don't succeed in a whole book.<br/><br/>The Dutch translation that I read, had a horrible title. The poetical Spanish title (Doce Cuentos Peregrinos, Twelve Pilgrim Stories) fitted exactly, because there are 12 stories, the rough drafts have traveled with Marquez to the different places where he li</span>
  <span id="freeText18265563903434714752" style="display:none">Marquez remains a great writer. While not every story in this bundle is equally enjoyable, they all show great mastery and the ability to draw interesting characters in a few lines, a feat in which some writers don't succeed in a whole book.<br /><br />The Dutch translation that I read, had a horrible title. The poetical Spanish title (Doce Cuentos Peregrinos, Twelve Pilgrim Stories) fitted exactly, because there are 12 stories, the rough drafts have traveled with Marquez to the different places where he lived and the stories are set at distant locations throughout Europe and Middle America. In Dutch they called this bundle: "The Lucky Summer of Mrs Forbes", which is the title of just one of the stories and certainly not the best, and has no bearing whatsoever on the general content. Why? No idea.<br /><br />Anyway, most stories are pleasant to read just because of the great diction. One I liked best was : "I only came to make a call". It is about a middle aged woman on her way to Barcelona, who enters a large and remote building to telephone her husband that she will be home a little later. Unfortunately, it turns out to be a mental institution for women and they mistake her for a new inmate. All attempts at escape are blocked by remorseless nurses. Together with the description of pure misery, Marquez manages to slip humour into this passage about this most heavily built nurse.<br /><br />(My apologies for the bad translation, it went from Spanish to Dutch into English, I'll just try to get it as close as possible:)<br /><br />"One look at her face sufficed to know that implorations would have no effect on the obsessed woman in uniform who, because of her incredible strength, was called Herculina. She was responsible for the difficult cases and two patients had already been strangled by her ice bear-like arm that was trained in 'killing by accident'. In the first case it was judged a misfortune. The second case was less clear, and a new event would result into a thorough investigation. The usual rumour was that she was a lost sheep from a notorious family who trailed behind her an obscure career of dubious incidents in several asylums in Spain."<br /><br />Marquez short stories are all strong enough to stand by themselves and are entertaining to read, with subtle humour and a touch of magic.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18265563903434714752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_197446206" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/197446206" />
    <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy"><img alt="Jenny (Reading Envy)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455391853p2/68030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/197446206?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny (Reading Envy)" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy">Jenny (Reading Envy)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Karen A.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=read2013">read2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=around-the-world">around-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer197446206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11887489144951331435">This was one of the books that had been on my to-read list the longest, and I chose it for my most recent <a href='http://readingenvy.blogspot.com/2013/07/book-speed-dating-2-pile.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>speed-dating project</a>. I was originally going to count it for my Around the World challenge, and still kind of am, but it doesn't take place in just one country. Quite the opposite, each story takes place in a different European country, often with displaced Latin Americans as characters.<br/><br/>It just isn't surprising that these stories come from the same author as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/760.Memories_of_My_Melancholy_Whores' title='Memories of My Melancholy Whores by Gabriel Garcí­a Márquez' rel='nofollow noopener'>Memories of My Melancholy Whores</a>,</span>
  <span id="freeText11887489144951331435" style="display:none">This was one of the books that had been on my to-read list the longest, and I chose it for my most recent <a href="http://readingenvy.blogspot.com/2013/07/book-speed-dating-2-pile.html" rel="nofollow noopener">speed-dating project</a>. I was originally going to count it for my Around the World challenge, and still kind of am, but it doesn't take place in just one country. Quite the opposite, each story takes place in a different European country, often with displaced Latin Americans as characters.<br /><br />It just isn't surprising that these stories come from the same author as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/760.Memories_of_My_Melancholy_Whores" title="Memories of My Melancholy Whores by Gabriel Garcí­a Márquez" rel="nofollow noopener">Memories of My Melancholy Whores</a>, because most of these stories find the storyteller looking back, at a country or an event, and there is quite a bit of nostalgia here. It <i>feels</i> like the author is old. My impressions may be a bit off, as the author is still alive and these stories were originally published in 1992. There is also a great deal of fantasy, magical realism, and horror. You never know when it is coming, and as a reader, that makes for better adventures in the pages.<br /><br />Story highlights:<br /><br /><i>The Saint</i> - This story bleeds over into fantasy, about a child who dies but does not decay, and her father does everything to try to get her canonized. <br /><br /><i>I Sell My Dreams</i> - A woman is remembered for her dream interpretations. I loved this!<br /><br /><i>I Only Came to Use the Phone</i> - Don't get on the wrong bus. Terrifying.<br /><br /><i>The Ghosts of August</i> - Takes place in Arezzo, a ghost story. <br /><br /><i>Maria dos Prazeres</i> - A retired prostitute prepares for her death, and I loved this line:<br />"After the unhurried supper and conversation, they made sendentary love from memory, which left both of them with a taste of disaster."<br /><br /><i>Light is Like Water</i> - What if you took a child's imagination to the logical conclusion?<br /><br /><i>The Trail of Your Blood in the Snow</i> - Oh, so sad.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11887489144951331435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1372334582" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1372334582" />
    <a title="Edward" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12933866-edward"><img alt="Edward" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444136022p2/12933866.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1372334582?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward" href="/user/show/12933866-edward">Edward</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140230963" href="/book/show/527193.Strange_Pilgrims">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12933866-edward?shelf=nobel-winners">nobel-winners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12933866-edward?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12933866-edward?shelf=short-story">short-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12933866-edward?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1372334582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2097488451370769002"><i>Strange Pilgrims</i> is a collection of short stories with an overarching theme: the experience of South American expatriates in Europe. While I could not connect personally to the theme, I did enjoy the stories, which were imaginative and expertly constructed. The stories deal with alienation, confusion, and death, though they do so with a sort of melancholy playfulness. They are light on magical realism elements (though these elements do feature in some stories, most notably in <i>Light is Like Water</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2097488451370769002" style="display:none"><i>Strange Pilgrims</i> is a collection of short stories with an overarching theme: the experience of South American expatriates in Europe. While I could not connect personally to the theme, I did enjoy the stories, which were imaginative and expertly constructed. The stories deal with alienation, confusion, and death, though they do so with a sort of melancholy playfulness. They are light on magical realism elements (though these elements do feature in some stories, most notably in <i>Light is Like Water</i>), opting for a more straightforward, albeit whimsical, approach to storytelling.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2097488451370769002" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95845425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer136707520068503313">Like Márquez always, the definitive definition of “splendid.” <br/><br/>He made a note of something in the prologue, though, that caught my interest: on the decades he worked on these stories, on how they unexpectedly drove him with just as much frustration as work on a novel: <br/><br/>“The effort involved in writing a short story is as intense as beginning a novel, where everything must be defined in the first paragraph: structure, tone, style, rhythm, length, and sometimes even the personality of a character. Al</span>
  <span id="freeText136707520068503313" style="display:none">Like Márquez always, the definitive definition of “splendid.” <br /><br />He made a note of something in the prologue, though, that caught my interest: on the decades he worked on these stories, on how they unexpectedly drove him with just as much frustration as work on a novel: <br /><br />“The effort involved in writing a short story is as intense as beginning a novel, where everything must be defined in the first paragraph: structure, tone, style, rhythm, length, and sometimes even the personality of a character. All the rest is the pleasure of writing, the most intimate, solitary pleasure one can imagine (…) But a story has no beginning, no end: Either it works or it doesn’t.”<br /><br />Which is exactly what I like to hear, both in line and in contrast with Cormac McCarthy <a href="http://online.wsj.com/article/SB10001424052748704576204574529703577274572.html" rel="nofollow noopener">when he said</a>, “I’m not interested in writing short stories. Anything that doesn’t take years of your life and drive you to suicide hardly seems worth doing.”<br /><br />As when I first read that, I agree in part: up to the fact that— as Márquez is saying here— short stories have just as much right, and power, to willfully wrestle away decades of your life.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2557987175" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2557987175" />
    <a title="Adarsh Chauhan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30211354-adarsh-chauhan"><img alt="Adarsh Chauhan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584163245p2/30211354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2557987175?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adarsh Chauhan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adarsh Chauhan" href="/user/show/30211354-adarsh-chauhan">Adarsh Chauhan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2557987175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14266583829310815851">I feel that I keep coming back to Marquez's melancholy-soaked stories time and again because I have not found any other author whose stories have that indelible impression and evocation of sorrowful sympathy as much as Marquez's. The short stories in this collection have less of his realist magical aspects than his other usual novel stories but it possesses the same unique quality in terms of conjuring and delivery. Reading one after the other, the readers gets the harmony of the short compositi</span>
  <span id="freeText14266583829310815851" style="display:none">I feel that I keep coming back to Marquez's melancholy-soaked stories time and again because I have not found any other author whose stories have that indelible impression and evocation of sorrowful sympathy as much as Marquez's. The short stories in this collection have less of his realist magical aspects than his other usual novel stories but it possesses the same unique quality in terms of conjuring and delivery. Reading one after the other, the readers gets the harmony of the short compositions and see the bigger picture - the experience of foreignness that one finds himself in when put far away in lands unknown and different from one's origins and memories. The stories here complete the mosaic of this experience with sorrowfulness, paranoia, pitifulness, uncertainty, and despite everything, tenacity and a feeling of moving on. The predicaments that his characters usually find themselves in even evoke a sympathetic humour and I somehow remembered lines (not exact) from Heinlein's <i>Stranger in a Strange Land</i> (may be triggered by the keyword 'stranger') while reading this book:<br /><br />“<i>I've found out why people laugh. They laugh because it hurts so much . . . because it's the only thing that'll make it stop hurting.</i>”<br /><br />Probably Marquez aims at achieving this reflection in the readers through humour by creating characters who are victims of some times their circumstances, and at other times, of their own shortcomings. My favourite stories from this collection were: "María dos Prazeres", "The Trail of Your Blood in the Snow", "I Only Came To Use The Phone" and "The Saint". Marquez is undoubtedly an important author of fiction with a beauty in writing influenced by his Latin American origins.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14266583829310815851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2535750809" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2535750809" />
    <a title="Daniel Chaikin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18695911-daniel-chaikin"><img alt="Daniel Chaikin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534027159p2/18695911.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2535750809?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel Chaikin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel Chaikin" href="/user/show/18695911-daniel-chaikin">Daniel Chaikin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2535750809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2305038989038815829">51. <b>Strange Pilgrims : Twelve Stories by Gabriel García Márquez</b><br/><b>translation</b>: 1993, by Edith Grossman<br/><b>originally published</b>: 1992<br/><b>format</b>: 195 page paperback<br/><b>acquired</b>: August<br/><b>read</b>: Sep 18-25<br/><b>rating</b>: 3½<br/><br/>Márquez presents these twelve stories as a remnant rescued from a lost collection. His introduction tells of 64 story ideas, with notes and sketches that were kept in a notebook and lost together with it. He selected these twelve for how they interact with each other, and then re-wrote them for this collect</span>
  <span id="freeText2305038989038815829" style="display:none">51. <b>Strange Pilgrims : Twelve Stories by Gabriel García Márquez</b><br /><b>translation</b>: 1993, by Edith Grossman<br /><b>originally published</b>: 1992<br /><b>format</b>: 195 page paperback<br /><b>acquired</b>: August<br /><b>read</b>: Sep 18-25<br /><b>rating</b>: 3½<br /><br />Márquez presents these twelve stories as a remnant rescued from a lost collection. His introduction tells of 64 story ideas, with notes and sketches that were kept in a notebook and lost together with it. He selected these twelve for how they interact with each other, and then re-wrote them for this collection. Each story is dated to when he began writing them, an odd choice, especially as these dates are printed at the end of the story. But, I think it's significant that all twelve dates are from before he won the Nobel Prize in late 1982.<br /><br />It's kind of sad how little these stories sparked my thinking. They are elegant and so carefully written, all twelve have wonderful openings and read effortlessly. These are polished works. The first story, on a deposed and exiled Caribbean president undergoing a medical procedure in Switzerland, has hung around. And the one titled <i>I Sell My Dreams</i>, well it's a wonderful title. But the rest, the haunted house, the depression from the Spanish sea side wind, and so forth, largely dissipated as I finished them. They left me thinking Márquez had, by his point, become too safe a writer, so worried about how clean his work was that he was no longer provoking, or making the reader uncomfortable. That analysis, if I can call it that, is unfair and it doesn't apply to his other later works that I've read, although it may capture an aspect of them. Márquez leans toward a quiet clean formality in style. These twelve stories stand mainly as polished sketches. I doubt anyone will mind picking this book up and reading through it, but I suspect many other readers will, like me, then just move on to the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2305038989038815829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1804576" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1804576" />
    <a title="Pamela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/124136-pamela"><img alt="Pamela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1189375143p2/124136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1804576?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pamela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pamela" href="/user/show/124136-pamela">Pamela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1804576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13613419163970367801">Strange Pilgrims is a collection of short stories that Gabriel Garcia Marquez had rattling around his brain. The stories hardly carry the heft and magic of his novels, but some of them are quite striking. "I Only Came to Use the Phone" and "The Trail of Your Blood in the Snow" are both haunting stories about husbands searching for wives who have suddenly disappeared. In the former, the wife has been mistakenly locked in a mental hospital whose bureaucracies and catch-22s prevent her from leaving</span>
  <span id="freeText13613419163970367801" style="display:none">Strange Pilgrims is a collection of short stories that Gabriel Garcia Marquez had rattling around his brain. The stories hardly carry the heft and magic of his novels, but some of them are quite striking. "I Only Came to Use the Phone" and "The Trail of Your Blood in the Snow" are both haunting stories about husbands searching for wives who have suddenly disappeared. In the former, the wife has been mistakenly locked in a mental hospital whose bureaucracies and catch-22s prevent her from leaving. In the latter, the wife bleeds to death in a hospital while the husband is given the run-around. Why Marquez uses the same terrifying plot line for two stories in a rather small short story collection (12 stories in all) is a subject of interesting speculation. In the end, I'd recommend this collection for completists, but hardly for the newcomer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13613419163970367801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10756450201782374628" style="display:none">One of those feelings you can't shake, when you feel so alone in a foreign city. That feeling of isolation, completely lost. <div id="review_3608764502" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3608764502" />
    <a title="Ana Nagham" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74574637-ana-nagham"><img alt="Ana Nagham" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606154759p2/74574637.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1801491277432574443">I have read some of this book as a Penguin 60, in which four of these were re-published.<br/><br/>Like that review, I have stuck it is a spoiler, as with stories so short it is hard not to give plot information... but no more than other reviews have... and I don't think I have spoiled them...<br/><br/>As it explains on the back of my edition - 12 stories of Latin Americans in Europe, Linked by themes of displacement and exile, vivid stories of love loneliness, death and memories of past life.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[<br/>Bon Voya</span></span>
  <span id="freeText1801491277432574443" style="display:none">I have read some of this book as a Penguin 60, in which four of these were re-published.<br /><br />Like that review, I have stuck it is a spoiler, as with stories so short it is hard not to give plot information... but no more than other reviews have... and I don't think I have spoiled them...<br /><br />As it explains on the back of my edition - 12 stories of Latin Americans in Europe, Linked by themes of displacement and exile, vivid stories of love loneliness, death and memories of past life.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />Bon Voyage Mr President - tells of an ousted South American President, in Geneva for medical treatment, and living a paupers life. His interactions with a former countryman and his wife end very different from how they were anticipated at their meeting. 4.5/5.<br /><br />The Saint - the story of a child who dies but does not decay, and her father does everything to try to get her canonized. Fantasy fiction. 3/5.<br /><br />Sleeping Beauty on the Airplane - a tale of love at first sight, unrequited love, and a tale of inaction. 3.5/5.<br /><br />I sell My Dreams - A woman is remembered for her dream interpretations. 2.5/5.<br /><br />'I Only Came to Use the Phone' - a horror story of circumstance. A woman whose car breaks down attempts to solicit help - to use their telephone, only to be locked away with the other lunatics. 4/5.<br /><br />The Ghosts of August - a short ghost story about a haunted house. 3/5.<br /><br />Maria dos Prazeres - A retired prostitute prepares for her death. 2.5/5<br /><br />Seventeen Poisoned Englishmen - A religious woman, an unsuccessful pilgrimage to meet the pope stays in a hotel, a floor above seventeen Englishmen. 2/5.<br /><br />Tramontana - Events in the tramontana , a harsh land wind. 1.5/5.<br /><br />Miss Forbes Summer of Happiness - Children on holidays at the family holiday house at the beach rebel against a nanny, but the result is not the one they expected. 3/5.<br /><br />Light is Like Water - Magical realism in the wild imagination of two children. I have never really been a huge fan of magical realism presented as a story in a 'normal setting'. One of the boys asks why the lights went on with just a flick of the switch, and the narrator flippantly responds, “Light is like water. You turn the tap and out it comes.” After that the boys ask their parents for a boat, and each time their parents go out they break a light-bulb and let light pour out to a depth of three feet, and go sailing around the house. 2/5<br /><br />The Trail of Your Blood in the Snow - On a honeymoon trip, a young bride pricks her finger on a rose, and during a drive across France cannot locate a pharmacy for assistance. Arriving in Paris, they rush to the hospital, and at the emergency ward, she is admitted quickly, while her husband is left to find a place to stay. On returning he is told visiting is only on Tuesdays, the next Tuesday being 6 days away. The story outlines the run around he gets as a non-French speaker in a city he is unfamiliar with. 4/5.<br /><br />(hide spoiler)]<br /><br />I think an overall 3.5, rounded up to 4 stars. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_149388084" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/149388084" />
    <a title="Stephanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/245640-stephanie"><img alt="Stephanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333847870p2/245640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/149388084?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie" href="/user/show/245640-stephanie">Stephanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140239409" href="/book/show/452153.Strange_Pilgrims">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer149388084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8205423299135559302">After the short story "The Handsomest Drowned Man in the World," which has been an enchanting but brief introduction to Marquez, _Strange Pilgrims_ is my first real encounter with his writing, which is a steady-handed mix of precision and warmth. His story-telling is urbane, evoking a 20th century past nether-world in which what for a sub-urban American is strangeness (the migrating pain of an ousted president-in-exile, the weightless body of a saint, a woman who makes a living by selling her dr</span>
  <span id="freeText8205423299135559302" style="display:none">After the short story "The Handsomest Drowned Man in the World," which has been an enchanting but brief introduction to Marquez, _Strange Pilgrims_ is my first real encounter with his writing, which is a steady-handed mix of precision and warmth. His story-telling is urbane, evoking a 20th century past nether-world in which what for a sub-urban American is strangeness (the migrating pain of an ousted president-in-exile, the weightless body of a saint, a woman who makes a living by selling her dreams, an endearing little dog who has been trained to cry) that seems totally natural--his "magical realism," but maybe only for the blockheaded reader (me as well) will it be more magical than real. The characters are all alluring, each for different reasons, but all because they are one with the realities of their stories. The atmosphere of each city--Geneva, Rome, Barcelona, Madrid, Paris, etc.--is rendered in its beauty and stench with dispassionate reverie. The author occasionally but very naturally intervenes to mention where he picked up the story or even to relate an interaction with his characters, situating himself as one of them, even as he writes about himself in a kind of disguise. All of it adds to a sum of measured skill, a trustworthy story-teller, and, for me, the best kind of reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8205423299135559302" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1755668575" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1755668575" />
    <a title="Amrita Saju" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46596337-amrita-saju"><img alt="Amrita Saju" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502603782p2/46596337.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1755668575?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amrita Saju" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amrita Saju" href="/user/show/46596337-amrita-saju">Amrita Saju</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1755668575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14697954392738204493">I started reading 'Strange Pilgrims' because I simply loved 'Love in the time of cholera' and was hoping to get another such read from Marquez. Yes, it's very similarly intense, but most of these stories are so depressing, especially the last one titled 'The Trail of Your Blood in the Snow', I didn't want it to end that way. Not that I don't enjoy that kind of writing, where even a tragedy is very beautiful to read, but I just wanted a happy ending. Is it too much to ask for that? <br/>In most of my </span>
  <span id="freeText14697954392738204493" style="display:none">I started reading 'Strange Pilgrims' because I simply loved 'Love in the time of cholera' and was hoping to get another such read from Marquez. Yes, it's very similarly intense, but most of these stories are so depressing, especially the last one titled 'The Trail of Your Blood in the Snow', I didn't want it to end that way. Not that I don't enjoy that kind of writing, where even a tragedy is very beautiful to read, but I just wanted a happy ending. Is it too much to ask for that? <br />In most of my previous experiences (though very few), I've found how short stories are always more sadder, intense and some so metaphorical that I don't understand them at all. I would like to attribute this incomprehensible state of my mind to the limited exposure I have to such intense writings. There was one such story in this book too that I found absolutely indecipherable; it was titled 'Light is like Water'. Someday I hope someone can take me through Marquez's point on that piece of writing.<br />This obviously won't stop me from wanting to read more of the author's works, because even though not a very interesting one, this was certainly a 'rich in vocabulary', 'enriched in deeper emotions' kind of a read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14697954392738204493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_168283044" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168283044" />
    <a title="Francisco" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4157824-francisco"><img alt="Francisco" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573522572p2/4157824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168283044?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Francisco" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Francisco" href="/user/show/4157824-francisco">Francisco</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168283044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12139460913218953161">Beautiful book. I particularly enjoyed The Trail of Your Blood in the Snow and "I Only Came to Use the Phone" . I think this book is quite witty, because it makes you fall in love with the characters before you even realize it, and then you can't really stop reading. Every character has been draw, with such tenderness and humanity, you start thinking they might be your neighbors, or that you would love them as friends. The Trail of Your Blood in the Snow is exceptional, because it speaks of a lo</span>
  <span id="freeText12139460913218953161" style="display:none">Beautiful book. I particularly enjoyed The Trail of Your Blood in the Snow and "I Only Came to Use the Phone" . I think this book is quite witty, because it makes you fall in love with the characters before you even realize it, and then you can't really stop reading. Every character has been draw, with such tenderness and humanity, you start thinking they might be your neighbors, or that you would love them as friends. The Trail of Your Blood in the Snow is exceptional, because it speaks of a love so passionate, and so ephemeral, you can´t help but wonder if it would have endured through time. I highly recommend this book to those that enjoy human-like stories that are dipped in the most delicious irony.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12139460913218953161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_218028747" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/218028747" />
    <a title="Rosemary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4723954-rosemary"><img alt="Rosemary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514914620p2/4723954.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/218028747?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rosemary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rosemary" href="/user/show/4723954-rosemary">Rosemary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141032498" href="/book/show/2150154.Strange_Pilgrims">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer218028747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14951818953736918369">Twelve short stories of the experiences of people from Latin America in Europe - although the prologue, telling how the stories evolved out of notes taken by GGM when he was living in Europe himself, almost makes a thirteenth story. They're whimsical and engaging, although often tragic, with elements of magical realism and/or horror. A theme is people being out of sync with their environment in one way or another, which I suppose is natural for both the emigré and the tourist experience.<br/><br/>I enjoye</span>
  <span id="freeText14951818953736918369" style="display:none">Twelve short stories of the experiences of people from Latin America in Europe - although the prologue, telling how the stories evolved out of notes taken by GGM when he was living in Europe himself, almost makes a thirteenth story. They're whimsical and engaging, although often tragic, with elements of magical realism and/or horror. A theme is people being out of sync with their environment in one way or another, which I suppose is natural for both the emigré and the tourist experience.<br /><br />I enjoyed them all, but my favourites were <i>Maria dos Prazeres</i> who teaches her dog to go cry on her future grave, and <i>Miss Forbes' Summer of Happiness</i> for the two small boys who rebel against their strict governess.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14951818953736918369" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1353229469" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1353229469" />
    <a title="Aurora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7028532-aurora"><img alt="Aurora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1322010013p2/7028532.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1353229469?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aurora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aurora" href="/user/show/7028532-aurora">Aurora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1353229469" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11660592795230329082">This is the second work by Marquez I have read, and it is rare to find authors who are good at both novels and short stories, so I was not sure what to expect. What I got was, like A Hundred Years of Solitude, stories and characters that have crept back into my mind weeks and months after reading them. To say that I love Marquez's lack of clarity in writing may sound weird, but I think it honestly reflects how we can never truly know what another person is thinking, what motivates them, how they</span>
  <span id="freeText11660592795230329082" style="display:none">This is the second work by Marquez I have read, and it is rare to find authors who are good at both novels and short stories, so I was not sure what to expect. What I got was, like A Hundred Years of Solitude, stories and characters that have crept back into my mind weeks and months after reading them. To say that I love Marquez's lack of clarity in writing may sound weird, but I think it honestly reflects how we can never truly know what another person is thinking, what motivates them, how they feel. Marquez's refusal to give away everything about a character actually helps to make them more real through their mystery. Not every author can do this successfully, which is one of the reasons I love his writing. Look forward to reading more!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11660592795230329082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1585200669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15713360597059048171">This was part of my Author's birthday month read. Marquez was born in March so like me he's a Pisces, yes!!<br/><br/>I haven't read many short stories and I wasn't sure how I would feel about this one. I can honestly say out of these 12 stories there were only about 3-4 that I wasn't too fond of but otherwise I really enjoyed the rest. My issue with short stories is that of course it leaves me wanting more and that's what happened in this case. Overall, I loved the characters, the scenery, the writing, th</span>
  <span id="freeText15713360597059048171" style="display:none">This was part of my Author's birthday month read. Marquez was born in March so like me he's a Pisces, yes!!<br /><br />I haven't read many short stories and I wasn't sure how I would feel about this one. I can honestly say out of these 12 stories there were only about 3-4 that I wasn't too fond of but otherwise I really enjoyed the rest. My issue with short stories is that of course it leaves me wanting more and that's what happened in this case. Overall, I loved the characters, the scenery, the writing, the stories were thought provoking and some of the endings made me feel like I was in the Twilight zone. Definitely recommend. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EvtDVsiNmeBm2sr8s7BJb6dD2eeu2Z+S9fI+CdILfa0HvWhFTn8pqBCHp22+5ljQHFQYZpQ0iYTcIEqmns/hTA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZJ4PjIRFAmFghAue5N6FdNs+8ws0ZolZQCAHTE+x/QRx2CSfAreyKRbZZg/piJTLYCkyig6Ln09p8nPjA3Vh5Q==')})
  }

Para quien todavía no la leyó, El túnel es la mejor introducción al univ<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText576395464871805650\" style=\"display:none\">Breve e intensa novela publicada en 1948, este logrado fruto de la denominada &quot;literatura existencial&quot; le dio a su autor un reconocimiento que traspasó las fronteras nacionales. Para quien todavía no la leyó, El túnel es la mejor introducción al universo prodigioso de Ernesto Sábato; para quien la conoce, un clásico de las letras del continente, una historia sobre el drama del hombre arrojado en el sinsentido más doloroso: la conciencia de la nada. \nEl narrador describe una historia de amor y muerte en la que muestra la soledad del individuo contemporáneo. No están ausentes de esta trama policial y de suspenso, la locura y la increíble reflexión del protagonista, el pintor Juan Pablo Castel, debatiéndose por comprender las causas que lo arrastraron a matar a la mujer que amaba, María Iribarne, y que era su única vía de salvación. En este alucinante drama de la vida interior, seres intrincados en la bestial búsqueda de comprensión ceden a la mentira, la hipocresía y los celos desmedidos hasta el crimen más inexplicable. Aventura amorosa, aventura onírica, aventura del ser que dan testimonio de un asesinato, de cierta memoria culpable y de una valiente introspección. \nTécnicamente perfecta y de lectura apasionante, El túnel excede el negativismo ácido de Sartre y la frenética huida hacia el vacío que plantea El extranjero de Camus, pero tiene de esos dos maestros literarios la impronta genial que hace de la       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/13450.Gabriel_Garc_a_M_rquez">About Gabriel García Márquez</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/13450.Gabriel_Garc_a_M_rquez"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1588856705p3/13450.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/13450.Gabriel_Garc_a_M_rquez">Gabriel García Márquez
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
29,386
followers
</div>

</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9122932065635857605">Gabriel José de la Concordia Garcí­a Márquez was a Colombian novelist, short-story writer, screenwriter and journalist. Garcí­a Márquez, familiarly known as "Gabo" in his native country, was considered one of the most significant authors of the 20th century. In 1982, he was awarded the Nobel Prize in Literature.<br/><br/>He studied at the University of Bogotá and later worked as a reporter for the Colombian</span>
  <span id="freeText9122932065635857605" style="display:none">Gabriel José de la Concordia Garcí­a Márquez was a Colombian novelist, short-story writer, screenwriter and journalist. Garcí­a Márquez, familiarly known as "Gabo" in his native country, was considered one of the most significant authors of the 20th century. In 1982, he was awarded the Nobel Prize in Literature.<br /><br />He studied at the University of Bogotá and later worked as a reporter for the Colombian newspaper <i>El Espectador</i> and as a foreign correspondent in Rome, Paris, Barcelona, Caracas, and New York. He wrote many acclaimed non-fiction works and short stories, but is best-known for his novels, such as <i>One Hundred Years of Solitude</i> (1967) and <i>Love in the Time of Cholera</i> (1985). His works have achieved significant critical acclaim and widespread commercial success, most notably for popularizing a literary style labeled as magical realism, which uses magical elements and events in order to explain real experiences. Some of his works are set in a fictional village called Macondo, and most of them express the theme of solitude.<br /><br />Having previously written shorter fiction and screenplays, García Márquez sequestered himself away in his Mexico City home for an extended period of time to complete his novel <i>Cien años de soledad</i>, or <i>One Hundred Years of Solitude</i>, published in 1967. The author drew international acclaim for the work, which ultimately sold tens of millions of copies worldwide. García Márquez is credited with helping introduce an array of readers to magical realism, a genre that combines more conventional storytelling forms with vivid, layers of fantasy.<br /><br />Another one of his novels, <i>El amor en los tiempos del cólera</i> (1985), or <i>Love in the Time of Cholera</i>, drew a large global audience as well. The work was partially based on his parents' courtship and was adapted into a 2007 film starring Javier Bardem. García Márquez wrote seven novels during his life, with additional titles that include <i>El general en su laberinto</i> (1989), or <i>The General in His Labyrinth</i>, and <i>Del amor y otros demonios</i> (1994), or <i>Of Love and Other Demons</i>.<br /><br />(Arabic: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5029628._" rel="nofollow noopener">جابرييل جارسيا ماركيز</a>) (Hebrew: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7091051._" rel="nofollow noopener">גבריאל גארסיה מרקס</a>) </span>
  <a data-text-id="9122932065635857605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
